GT: c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) - c4*(T - c5) + c6*(T - c7)*log(epsilon + c8)

Let \(e=\epsilon\). Rewrite the GT in a structural way.

### Ground Truth (fixed function)
\[
\text{GT}(e,T)=96.8294\,e\Big(-0.00975241\,(T-352.1818)+1\Big)\;-\;0.478482\,(T-352.1818)\;+\;8.06201\,(T-352.1818)\log(e+1)
\]

Expand by separating \(T\)-dependence:

- The first term is **bilinear** in \(e\) and \(T\):  
  \(96.8294\,e\big(1-0.00975241\,T+0.00975241\cdot 352.1818\big)\)  
  so it contains an \(eT\) term and an \(e\) term.
- The second term is **linear in \(T\)** plus a constant.
- The third term is \((T-352.1818)\log(e+1)\): i.e. it contains
  - a \(T\log(e+1)\) term, and
  - a \(-352.1818\log(e+1)\) term (a pure \(\log(e+1)\) term independent of \(T\)).

So GT necessarily contains all of these functional “atoms” with nonzero coefficients:
1) \(eT\)  
2) \(e\)  
3) \(T\)  
4) constant  
5) \(T\log(e+1)\)  
6) \(\log(e+1)\) (pure, not multiplied by \(T\))  

Also, GT uses \(\log(e+1)\) (not \(\log|e|\), not \(\log(1+c|e|)\) unless exactly reducible to \(\log(e+1)\) for all real \(e\), which it is not).
